Debating jumping back into destiny
I love Destiny 2 and I've always loved Destiny as a series (Except Red War that was a spit in the face). And now that it feels they have their footing without Activision breathing down their necks and money from Sony, it truly feels like they know what they're doing. I hear from everyone that the UI and starting is super confusing but as a veteran since a little before Taken King I don't see it but can understand that if so many people are saying that, it must be true.  However the story is amazing (except for a few things they _still_ are holding close to their chest and makes the story feel hollow in areas) and is the second biggest inspiration for me in my writing. The music is the best in media. Period. There are few songs in Destiny I'd call 'bad', and most if not all of them have been removed so Nice. And the gunplay is just. Just the best. Even other supposed "Good gunplay" is dwarfed by Destiny 2. Fallout, the Mass Effect trilogy, High on Life (wat?), various Call of Duty and Battlefield games, Overwatch, Valorant, the Metroid Prime trilogy, and more. All of them are boring and limiting compared to the utter freedom Destiny's classes, subclasses, weapons, abilities, stats, armor sets, artifacts, perks, mods, and more all make me feel like I can be anything I want to be.  There's a reason I'm in the top 10% of players in playtime. Because it's fun, addicting, and frankly, sometimes a better friend and family member than the real ones where sometimes, especially during the hardest times of my life (Well also that I just turned 18 and have yet to get my life off the ground yet). Destiny 2 for me is therapy. It allows me to not worry about my anxieties, my fears, my ADHD, my problems. It allows me to escape my issues and just play, fight, win, kill. To enjoy a world I have never stopped loving since I first read about it on my dad's phone while in the line for a Disneyland ride at 10 PM in the now far off year of 2016.  Am I biased to the extreme to this game? Yeah, definitely. I won't ever deny that. I love it and it's as close to me as any media can be, but I know there's objective positives and that this game is *objectively* a good game now. For everyone? No. Heck, my brother finds it boring, confusing, and repetitive. But the last thing you can say about Destiny 2 is that it is not loved by its owners and fanbase.  The poor thing was born way too early, mishandled by two fighting parents over what it should be for years, the better parent won custody but was just as lost as Destiny, leading to even more mishandling, but Bungie just needed to find their footing and truly show they love the game. Now Destiny has never been in a better place and I am so happy to see such a pitiful game now outshines every other MMO out there and is consistently on Steam's top ten most played games alone, not even factoring the other consoles' playerbase.  Started caring about the series before I was even a teenager, now I'm an adult and looking back, I wouldn't have traded anything for those memories of this franchise. It truly is special, even if it is to just me and me alone. I might leave after The Final Shape like I did Marvel and Endgame. The story _I_ grew up with will be done and therefor it would be time for me to move on. But who knows? Maybe Destiny will be something I'll be telling my kids about.

Cynical former player here (late to the party here but just showed up in my feed).  I loved just logging in to shoot things.  But here is the structure under the patterns that results in the current state of the game: the developers cannot keep up with demand for new and entertaining game content (maps, missions, playlist activities, dungeons, raids etc).  So they constantly shift around  (or add) rules, currencies, progress systems, abilities, weapons, and so on, in order to keep existing players interested enough to keep playing.  They are always "changing the sandbox" (and that can be seen in a positive light by existing players).   These changes always throws players out of the routines they already play the game with.  The players have to adjust, and learn the newest best tactics, and make new progress.  For me that robs the sense of accomplishment for making any progress.  And I wonder how much development time goes to moving the rug out from under players versus actually developing playable game content?  This is a one-sided take (there are good reasons to adjust the sandbox) but I can't un-think the idea that they are just deliberately making players adjust to changes as a filler for "not enough content." ogh... the number of factually incorrect info in this vid pain me xD though it is not your fault dude. The game DOES have confusing experience for new players. The campaign of WQ on "normal" difficulty is braindead easy, that's why "legendary" difficulty is HIGHLY advised for balanced challenging experience where you have to think and plan ahead. Hi destiny 1 veteran here, and destiny 2 fan that has been playing since beyond light here to help to shed some light (pun intended) on the destiny 2 new light experience as I understand that it can be very overwhelming at first and I hope this comment helps clear some things up for your proper destiny 2 review and I'm sure you figured some of this stuff by now. When starting out the best things to focus on are vanguard and gambit related activities while dipping your toes in crucible every now and then as it can be a very unbalanced experience. In regarding to leveling up every tuesday there is whats called a weekly reset which refreshes pinnacle activities and the bright dust store (the free eververse store option) Pinnacle activities fall under gambit, crucible, and vanguard strikes. When you complete a pinnacle quest (which is usually complete 3 matches or missions) you are given pinnacle loot which has a high power level and you can either use the item or infuse it to armor or weapons that you currently have. Which can end up accumulating and bringing up your guardians power level. You can infuse by using upgrade modules which u can get from either leveling up vendors such as shaxx, zavala, and drifter, buying them from ada-1 or the gunsmith, or from the battle pass. For the most part they have gotten rid of the vendor currency like tokens or gunsmith materials so instead of leveling up vendors through tokens you just do activities and it will automatically level them up. As we all know the true excitement in destiny 2 is endgame activities such as raid and dungeons. You already did a dungeon with the grasp of avarice (the pirate themed mission you did) but there are other dungeons such as prophecy, shattered throne and pit of heresy. With the weekly reset these dungeons and the raids will rotate and each week a different dungeon or raid will drop pinnacle gear. So one week it will be vault of glass and prophecy, and another week it will be kings fall and grasp of avarice that will drop pinnacle loot. DO NOT MAIN ONE CHARACTER FOREVER! I cannot stress this enough, with someone that has ADHD it can be annoying to play the same character so remember to swap things up every now and then. For example I main hunter but this season I've been playing warlock and I've been enjoying the hell out of it. Dont forget to pick up bounties so you can level up vendors faster. If your gonna buy dlc do it in this order: witch queen, beyond light, lightfall, and shadowkeep. And if your gonna preorder lightfall see if you can get the deluxe edition as that will help save money in the long run as you wont have to worry about buying season passes which each season when they drop so you can hop right in. This game can be very grindy but if you were able to get into runescape then im sure you will do just fine in destiny 2. Now get in there guardian and enact xeno genocide so you can get that sweet sweet loot that is slightly different from the same gun that has different perks. If you have any other questions don't be afraid to ask.

They need to find a way to streamline the "new" player experience a lot more than it currently is, since as the game is rn, you basically need to have a "veteran" explain everyting about the game, just so you can even have a chance of understanding how everything works.  They need to add things like:  a Weapons guide, explaining every weapon type, how they are used and what they are useful for + explaining everything about crafting weapons, how to unlock patterns and what the requirements to lvl said weapons are.  an Armor guide, explaining what each stat means and how they affect you, where to get stronger armor and what each mod slot means.  a Mod guide, that explains the different categories of mods, what they do and a basic overview of how to combine them.  an Ability guide, that has you using all of your main abilites for each class similar to how stasis is introduced to you in the beyond light expansion.  and most importantly an activity introduction video accessable ingame, that explains what every node in Orbit means, how to get where you want to go, where to find your missions and seasonal stuff, the fact that there is a quest archive where you can re pickup quests / missions you dismanteled and most importantly for people who want to dip their toes into harder content, what champions are, how to deal with them and where to expect them / also teaching people what modifiers are.  Man there's a shit ton of things you need to know about this game when looking at this list, specifically when you keep in mind, that this is a very basic list that doesn't even cover things like buff stacking, weapon perks, Adept and Artifice loot and plentitude of different things I just forgot about at this moment.

One of the main weaknesses of games with TONS of content is when returning/new players start up, it's super overwhelming and there isn't much in the way of tutorials unless a youtuber makes them. Path of Exile, Warframe, and Destiny all have this issue due to the fact that as more content is added, the more hurdles are added to keep players from progressing too fast, but at the same time the companies want the new/returning players to have access to the new content ASAP so they can unload their wallets into the game, so the new content is smashed into the player's face as soon as they load up rather than having them progress through the game like others did in the past.   I can only imagine being a dev and having to juggle between the new player experience and having to appease long time veterans of the game, so for any devs of games like this who read this - you have my empathy when it comes to having to do that kind of balancing.

I stopped playing because there's no real progression aside from story progression. Yes, our numbers continue to go up, but it's all meaningless. To elaborate, every season they increase the 'level' cap, but simultaneously increase the world 'level,' for lack of a better word, such that it's not unlike when first starting the game.  Weapons and gear are arbitrarily rendered useless by level limits and new gear must be obtained and leveled up to achieve the same efficacy as the previous season. This creates a significant time sink each season necessary to do, for example, end game content even if you were able to the previous season. I think the phrase, "short term pain, long term gain" is what you gotta know when getting in/back into Destiny. Even as a seasoned player from back in D1 with breaks in between, I often feel behind on some mechanics or what people feel is the current 'meta'. But the fact is that there's something for everyone: PvE, PvP, PvPvE, (finally a good) campaign, puzzle-like dungeons, intense raids. The game will ultimately leads you back to the RPG mechanics, but as you gain loot, it only becomes as complicated as the thought you put in. You can choose to take time and do buldcrafting, but you can also just play and equipt the loot you like. The nice thing is they've confirmed they're not sunsetting anything more. Sure, seasonal content may fade, but things fold into the loot pool. Campaigns are sticking, as are Raids and Dungeons (that Loot Cave thing you ran, Grasp of Avarice, is one of several now). And as such, once you learn a system, that means it retains relevancy. Subclasses are more dynamic now, there's a lot more synergies.   Mods for armor can do a lot once you learn what Combat Styles are (Warmind Cells, Charged with Light, and Elemental Wells), since it can help you form a build that changes a lot of your combat experience - and the next expansion is adding Loadouts so you don't have to use Destiny Item Manager (DIM) as a 3rd party system to manage loadouts and mod management for you.  Once you get past the terrible new player experience (They seriously just throw you in the deep end of pop-ups and content and say "have fun", rather than "Hey, let's get you started on some Strikes. Go learn what these playlists do. Couple matches in each. Oh, you entered an open world zone, here's what to do as a new player - bounties are here, these are patrols, etc..), the game can hook you on understanding these systems and getting into them.

One of my favorite aspects of Destiny 1 was the fact that it followed a similar logic to Syndrome: If everyone is OP, then nobody will be! Almost everyone who made it to max level had multiple pieces of gear that broke game mechanics in some way or another and in most games would be considered entirely overpowered, but that was just the way of things in Destiny. It was glorious chaos, and I was all there for it! I remember when Destiny 2 launched and turned its back on that philosophy entirely, and it was sad indeed. I've revisited the game a couple of times since then, but it never has captured my interest like the original. Maybe I'll get into it eventually, but in truth I don't think I'll ever enjoy it the way I enjoyed the original.

D1 beta, 8k hours (D1 + D2 combined) vet here. I fucking hate Bungie and what they do to this game, they charge a high premium for the content they sell but make decisions like making the game free to play WITH NO FUCKING ANTICHEAT. Every competetive playlist and even the casual PVP modes were totally unplayable for over a year, cheating was rampant and it's just something the players were expected to deal with.   They delayed their pinnacle PVP game mode trials under the notion of "we don't want to release it half baked" but when it  finally released it came out raw, the loot the matchmaking and the sandbox made it not worth playing. When the pool of players nose dived the difficulty of getting a flawless run skyrocketed, so the players devised a way to win trade and get some loot of a toxic sess pit of a game mode. Baring in mind that aimbot hacking had been a problem for over a year at this point and Bungo had done sweet FA to tackle the issue, when they learned people were win trading they immediately cracked down. Priorities are all fucked up.  The constant triple dipping of their dedicated fan base is a travesty of monetization. The game is free to play but to buy all the content ansd get access to every activity is a very high price, then you have the season pass which will cost you more dollars every few months and then theres the in game cosmetics store which again has a very high price on all its items because "we Bungie, we triple A, we charge triple A prices". If that wasnt bad enough a lot of us migrated from console to PC because of much better the game runs on this platofrm, you can link your profiles so you don't need to grind your weapons again but guess what? All the DLCs need to be bought for a second time. Don't even get me started on this gross "dungeon pass" bullshit they're trying to peddle now.  But the final nail in the coffin for me, and the reason i haven't played it since witch queen was their ethic towards balancing new weapons and abilities. Anyone remember stasis release and how it had to had 2 nerfs back to back (then it was buffed for some unfathomable reason?) and then had to be nerfed again? Anyone remember Gwisin vest? Anyone remember Lord of wolves (both times it was OP as fuck years apart) ? Mountaintop? High impact fusion rifles? Queenbreakers? Any heavy weapon in gambit? Vex mythoclast? Chaos Reach? The list is endless but we always thought it was just Bungie being inept at PVP balancing, this is untrue. They stated in a TWAB that they would always rather overbuff new weapons and abilities for no other reason than to make sales, then nerf them later into irrelevance. The PVP community will just adapt as we always force them to.  This game used to be 50-50 PVP/PVE, but now the casuals have it served up for them on a platter as 90% PVE and they love Bungo for it. So now im finally out and haven't looked back since and it feels great to be rid of this constant source of stress in my down time.   If you like PVP content stay the fuck away from Bungo and this game. Yours truly, a once dedicated player who's had enough of their fucking bullshit. From the bottom of my heart Bungo, FUCK YOU.

Destiny 2 is a fairly solid game with great and addicting gun play, like you've said. Perfect for players more interested in the PVE side of things that many games on the market can't seem to hold up to. But...  I think the community has kind of expressed some greviances with the series for some time. Primarily the toxic tendencies of the community, and the monetization aspect. Thankfully, first downside can be rectified by simply playing exclusively with some laid back friends or getting to know some players on a Discord server and teaming up that way. Second downside is thankfully fixed some by Bungie making it F2P, but the expansions and battle passes can still add up for those with tighter pockets.  Overall, it is a great game, and has made a massive turnaround since Witch Queen, but sadly for me, just didn't seem worth it to keep up with the game and put more money into it than I already had. I do have fond memories of my time playing though.

The new user experience for Destiny 2 right now is certainly rough, but it's nowhere near as bad as the Returning User Experience(tm), especially if you missed any of the now vaulted story content. I tried coming back to D2 last year and was so completely and utterly lost that I gave up after 25 minutes. As fun as the gameplay is, I had absolutely no idea what I should be doing first. Armor and weapons had seen huge changes and yet I had no idea whether any of the things I had equipped from years ago still had any value. There was nothing obvious to tell me what story quests, if any, I should make my way into. I felt like I was just dropped into the game with the expectation that I knew what I was doing, but considering that most of the initial content that existed to introduce new players to the characters, setting, and gameplay is gone, there wasn't even anything there for me to relearn what I'd forgotten, let alone find out what new things I needed to catch up on.  I suspect that you're better off starting with a fresh character than trying to jump back in with an old one.

Hey Act Man! Dunno if you'll ever see this but I hope you do!  I've been playing Destiny since the D1 BETA and I've loved every minute of it, through the good and the bad and I 100 percent agree with you, Destiny is far more entertaining with friends. One thing I will say is yes the new user experience is really quite daunting. But I have an idea on how that can be fixed and it takes an old idea from D1. I think Destiny shouldn't allow you to play the other campaigns until you played the previous ones. Say for example you want to play through Beyond Light, but you haven't played through Shadowkeep yet, well it should only pop up Shadowkeep campaign missions until you have completed them all. Then it'll allow you to play through the Beyond Light without overloading the player with so many campaign missions. This can also give you the choice the choice on what to focus on, do the endgame content for Shadowkeep and expand your knowledge on the world, or do that stuff later and start the next campaign. This would also give new players less things to overload on.  Second, I think the major tutorial quest stuff should come before allowing to do campaigns. Like explaining on what aspects and fragments are for your subclass, or what crafting material does what, how to level up weapons and armor, mods, etc. This would allow new players to be given a foundation they can work off of that they can master as they go through the campaign and can take further as they progress through endgame content. But these things have to be taught first before they anything, at least the fundamentals do.  3, stop ads. I get it, Bungie needs to make money, but sometimes it's gets in the way of you and the game and kinda sucks you out.  Other than that, I think Destiny is in a very great place right now, and can only get better. I think it just needs a tweak here and there. But overall, I love Destiny, it's world, it's story, and even it's deep dank lore you can read about in the in game lore cards!

Speaking as a player that's been a hardcore player since the D1 Alpha days, Destiny is an incredibly complex and unique game that is simultaneously inexcusably broken in various areas (e.g criminally broken and neglected PvP, rampant cheating, Gambit and content recycling and vaulting and even attracting new players) and breathtaking in its scope and design and gameplay. It's also influenced my life heavily and helped me form permanent friendships and develop better cooperation skills, so it shall always be close to my heart.  Something that we as fans ought to remember is that while we have many valid reasons to shit on the game, with how far mighty franchises like Halo and Battlefield have fallen and with how badly any game that has tried to be the "Destiny killer" has failed (I.e Anthem, Division, Avengers and Fallout 76 for instance) and with the sheer longevity of a game many wrote off at launch as dead both in 2014 AND 2017, we are reminded that there is something truly special and revolutionary in Destiny that has both influenced the industry and brought formerly PC exclusive experiences like raiding to us console plebs.

What I mean by that is that it is like starting your MCU journey with Captain America: Civil War.  In base game, the Traveller was asleep leaving Humanity standing alone against Fallen, Hive, Vex, and Cabal. The Awoken were sort of on our side, and Exos were complete mysteries. Now in Year 8, we have uncovered the mysteries of both Exos and Awoken, awakened the Traveller, killed several Gods, found new enemies in the Taken and Scorn, joined forces with the Eliksni House of Light and Cabal Empire, harnessed the power of the darkness in the form of Stasis, and now face the big baddie of the franchise ‚ÄòThe Witness‚Äô who has made his own army of similar forces. Planets have been consumed, replaced, destroyed. We‚Äôve travelled through time, recruited and mentored a guy that we once killed for killing our mentor. It‚Äôs crazy and Bungie said they want to reward players that stuck by them all this time. I love Destiny and feel like it's gotten much better over the past 2 years (I even have that PAX 2017 Emblem as well. <3) but I definitely don't disagree with a lot of the points you've brought up like how rough the new player experience is and throwing every pop-up from the past 6 months at you all at once being annoying when you just wanna play the game, you basically require an experienced guide to navigate through everything and tell you what's important.  But for me once you're able to get past that and get to more of the heftier content like the Dungeons and Raids where what weapons you bring and how you build starts to matter that's when you have one of the most satisfying PvE FPS games I've ever played in my opinion. (It's just getting to that point can be quite the struggle.) The Dungeons are particularly interesting because they're always designed to be able to be completed solo with their own Triumphs and flex emblems for doing so, but also aren't any easier either so you basically have to work 3x as hard to do those challenge runs.  And it's a mixed bag but I even personally enjoy the PvP with all its chaos, it's basically a game of avoiding everyone else's BS while inflicting your own BS on everyone else making it a sort of Mario Kart of PvP Shooters, and no other PvE-centric game has managed to get me invested in the PvP side of it like this game has. (And I think an important part of that is that PvP has unique rewards to draw you in that you can still take to other parts of the game if you get something you like.) Usually with games like this when they have a PvP mode on the side they are completely abandoned with hardly anyone playing them, like Warframe with its PvP Conclave comes to mind, so even if it's rough the fact that a game like this has such a dedicated PvP playerbase shows that there's at least a desire for people to want to play a game that combines tight FPS gameplay with RPG buildcrafting and mechanics. (Which I guess that's also sort of what CoD is, but it doesn't have that Sci-fi fantasy element to it.)

I weep for you.
Ah yes, destiny 2 the game i would be able to describe as shittiest and best game at same time.   Jokes aside, as someone who spent playing this game more then I would like to admit and have been playing since release of shadowkeep, New light experience was always dogshit (they did add "tutorial" for NEW players, not returning ones with Beyond light and addition of Cosmodrone). That has been a well known issue for now almost 2 full years. Lack of tutorial or guidance is an issue just as you said and I do not expect it to get better (actually i expect it to get worse). I do absolutely disagree that game changed much over the course of years, outside of raids and to a lesser extend dungeons and few notable strikes, its copy paste of "hordmod not hordmod" activity that gets very boring very fast (at the very least game did not change much since shadowkeep). Also this game DOES NOT ENCOURAGE OR REWARD solo play and if you want to play this game you should not start it solo or you will suffer.  Now what type of content destiny 2 has? We can split it in simply PvE, PvP and gambit.  PvE content most consist of grinding pinnacles or powerful engrams and artifact level so you are high enough light level for "high end" content. With powerful engram you can obtain gear "soft cap" of light level and with pinnacle "hard cap" which is always by 10 light levels higher then powerful cap. Pinnacle and powerful cap are increased by 10 each season (basically next season powerful cap will be previous season pinnacle cap). Why you do all that? So you can grind the best gear in game.... except not really. What this game does a lot and is managing to piss me off succsessfully  is that best PvE content might be locked behind High end PvP activity or other way around. Also the so called "Adept" variations of guns compare to normal ones are hardly worth farming. Sometimes top tier weapon is just a random world drop. Why do people do then high end activities such as Grandmaster nightfall strikes? Mostly for the Seal and bragging rights since there is no other reward really.  PvE can further be divided into Strikes, seasonal content, expansion campaign, dungeons raids, exotic quest and few more "off shots".  Vanguard playlist hold strikes and those are probably the easiest aspect of PvE content to start with, they are fairly linear and straightforward objective always being go in, shoot your way trough enemies, kill boss, get loot. What makes strikes more High end are difficulties and specifically Grandmaster strikes (but more on those later).  Expansion campaign is something new we got with witch queen and are more dynamic then strikes (but still follow the formula of get in, kill boss, get out) but are at least something a bit new (sadly engine limits are showing how simple still everything is).  Seasonal content is...... honestly the worst part of PvE content since it only serves as a gate wall to get new or reissued guns (more on that later). Also if you played 1 season seasonal content, you played them all. They are all hordemod not hordemod with different skin. Not every season is equally awful but at the very least i can say that storytelling in seasonal content IMPROVED DRASTICALLY in season of chosen in beyond light but ever since remained unchanged (and still most of story is told trough gatekeeping story each week and by lore books that are hidden). Quality of story also varies between seasons and is ONLY PLAYABLE if you own season pass.  Exotic quest are usually tied with season pass and/or with expansion, most quests are just a way to gatekeep you from exotic with a bit of a story that make you go from point A to point B  but there are some that break that monotony, most notable one being Dead messenger that has its dedicated mission with 2 difficulties for itself and its catalyst (they were more such quests but they were all Vaulted).  What ActMan played in the video and said he liked it is a dungeon which is, depending on the difficutly, mid to high end content that features a for now always 3 encounters and a bit of puzzles/sparrow driving between them. They stand different from strikes since they are a bit more then just "shoot boss, boss immune, kill adds that spawn, repeat until boss dead". There are total of 5 dungeons in the game and (for now) none were vaulted, 2 are free for new light players.  And at last we have raids which can be described as the pinnacle of destiny 2 (and are honestly they only content i personally give a shit about in this game anymore). Since beyond light and re release of Vault of Glass they feature Master difficulty for the most daring and normal difficulty for everyone else. Raids are unlike everything else so far, a 6 man PvE activities featuring actual mechanics, secrets, jumping puzzles and exclusive raid exotics (which some were Meta defining) and actual learning curve and mechanics outside of "just shoot lol". There is a lot to be said about each raid but I wont make this any longer than it needs to be, but I will say that there is atm total of 11 raids in destiny 2. 5 of them are vaulted 3 of them are free (2 of them are re issued d1 raid with some changes to mechanics and both of them have master difficulty) and 3 are locked behind expansion (each raid behind different one).  As for one offs, this is where destination content such as blindwell belongs and meanagering like activites belong. What are menagering like activities? Wellspring or any other 6 man PvE activity that is not a raid (that are somehow still all less original, more repetitive, less rewarding then menagering so therefore they hold such name, Menagering was season 7 (?) activity that is atm vaulted)  That wraps up PvE content, PvP we can split in casual pvp, Trials of osiris and iron banner. I will say in advance that I absolutely despite d2 PvP and hope for its death and bungie sure does not care much about it.  Casual pvp has several game modes but ill mention only one which is the main one (tho none are particularly good) and that is control aka typical capture zone (yea that is it).  Iron banner was the same until last season when they introduced capture flag to the game (yes really).  And last but certainly not much better is trials of osiris. Its an elimination style gamemod where you need to manually rez your team mates if they die, there is more but that sums it up well enough.  Now why do I loath d2 pvp and discourage anyone to ever play it? Well despite bungies lack of understanding of pvp and awful balance and controversies that you could write entire dictionary, all pvp (and actually entire game) is based on P2P connection............... Which makes for some awful games. Additionally, matchmaking is horseshit and bungie had tried (and failed) multiple times to improve it. Not to mention all the jank there is in PvP due to guns having aim assistance as a stat and so on.  And last but certainly not least shit is gambit.............. a mix of PvE and PvP that is completely awful and did not  got any major changes in more then 2 years.    Now that all that is said, as someone who has accumulated 3k h since games arrival on Steam and actually quited the game altogether during last season of beyond light (and would stay like that if friend did not gift me delux TWQ) I heavily discurage anyone from starting this game. Yep.... Destiny 2s biggest flaw is that it explains NOTHING.   For instance, that question you have about light level? Unless you're under leveled for something light level means nothing now because everything is scaled to your level if you're over what the game requires. It really only matters if you're doing harder content like Grandmaster strikes and master raids. The real thing you're striving for is to build up your arsenal, armor, armor mods and subclass builds so that you can do harder content. But the game NEVER tells you that.  But the gap in content is worse than you think. The days of just buying the yearly expansion and still knowing what's going on are long gone because major story beats are also in the seasonal content so if you don't buy those, you'll have no idea what's going on. Now don't get me wrong, they're a lot of bang for your buck, $10 four times a year gets you multiple seasonal activities, 5-12 new weapons with brand new perks to chase, a new armor set and armor ornament set to go along with it.... it's a good deal. Problem is that with every new expansion the previous year's seasons get thrown in the trash. Oops. There goes a full 4/5ths of the story.  And we're talking major stuff. Like us saving Saint-14 by altering the timeline. The Pyramid ships you saw at the end of Red War showing up and shoving the missing planets into black holes. The Cabal homeworld being destroyed by the Hive so Calus' daughter shows up and tries to force us into the Cabal, but we show that we aren't weak so we end up in an alliance instead. Some of the Fallen have decided to stop their pirate ways and have joined forces with us, forming a three way alliance. Calus has sided with the Darkness and all of his raids were a ploy to make us malleable enough to join his side. The list goes on. All content that is just gone and can't be accessed.  Bungie has been removing things because they need to keep the build of the game smaller so that they can roll out changes better and on that front they've succeeded. During Shadowkeep's year it took 6 months just to change an exotic because compiling the game's code was taking 24-36 hours whenever they made a change. Now we're getting fixes within a week.  Gameplay wise, D2 is in a fantastic state but the cohesion of the world its set in has gone to complete hell and its been like that for the last two years. Frankly, I wish we had just gone to D3 with Beyond Light and left D2 where it was. They sunset most of our stuff anyway so why not?
I really think you should make some videos on Dayz man, and just survival games in general like tarkov and scum. I just don't think they get enough attention and love. Generally the people who cover them are much smaller YouTubers.

This is 100% correct. The game, at its core, is amazing. The gunplay is extremely satisfying, the art direction is stunning, music is beautiful, it has a very rewarding gameplay loop, awesome and plentiful gear to make your character look however you want, and TONS of content to lose yourself in, but for a new player, I can imagine how incredibly confusing everything can be. Godroll weapons, stat distribution, build crafting etc. It's all either poorly explained by the game, or not at all. That's where the game probably loses most new players, especially with all the year one content being vaulted. Like you get this New Light quest and once you get through it, you just get thrown into the deep. No way of knowing which order the expansions are in, no deep explanation into core mechanics, just you against the world. This concept has been proven to be very popular. Look at FromSoft games. It's just that Destiny is NOT that type of game. Or well it is, but it has no right being it. There should be tutorials, clear indicators of where to start, recommended gear and pre-made loadouts+an in-game method of crafting your own loadout (which I know is finally coming with Lightfall). Like how the fuck is a new player supposed to know where to grind for materials such as enhancement prisms, ascendant shards etc? Or hell, even exotic gear? Seriously, how hard is it to add a tutorial that tells you "hey, enhancement prisms? You can grind those with Nightfalls. The higher the difficulty, the hugher the chance." Or "hey, want to grind out your exotic armor? Play legend lost sectors solo." The game should be full of things like that to point a new player in the right direction, but it isn't. You either find the game fun enough to look up all these things on your own, or you drop it, never to pick it up again. In this regard, Bungie REALLY needs to give the game a MASSIVE overhaul

it's a known issue that the new light (new player) experience is overwhelming af, but once you've got Ikora's foot in the door, and the game opens up, and things start making sense, it's fuckin awesome. a lot of things have been completely redone, what would've been D3 systems such as reworked armor, reworked subclasses, reworked weapons have instead been put into D2, rendering old gear near obsolete and leaving returning players thinking "wtf?" but it's all for the better in the end. Build crafting and tackling endgame activities with friends in a gorgeous sci-fi fantasy fps is an experience no other game offers. The power fantasy is real and you feel like a space magic wielding badass. For players that have stuck with the game over the years, it's much easier to see how seriously it has blossomed into something beautiful, not perfect, always striving to improve, but fucking beautiful. Also the lore is ridiculously rich and deep and seeing all the different characters and events come together and evolve over time is so very rewarding. If they improve upon the new light experience and offer catch up tutorials/videos for mechanics and the story there's little I could criticize.

So bungie made a deal with the devil to make the game relatively bug free, Trade all gameplay bugs for Telesto bugs. That gun breaks the game all the time. it was disabled at one point and RE ENABLED ITSELF VIA A BUG! Telesto is the 8th wonder of the world tbh.  Destiny is like Warframe in the sense of how new players experience it. If you play alone you'll have no fucking idea whats going on or how to navigate its many systems but if you have an experienced friend to act as a guide its much more enjoyable and accessible. Once you learn the game its much more manageable to play solo. I play story missions alone, pvp usually, and i do general grinding alone. But raiding, farming, completing challenges, and dungeons are all things i usually get people together for. The Loot Cave is a dungeon btw. If you like that you'd enjoy the other dungeons. The Shattered Throne was the first, being introduced with Forsaken and the Dreaming City. Pit of Heresy is another, that was introduced with Shadowkeep. The Prophecy is probably the most visually stunning out of them all. People love that dungeon and for good reason, its incredibly wild. The other dungeon just introduced with last season is Duality.   The gear in the H.E.L.M is like a "catch up" set. It cant overlevel you for the legendary witch queen campaign because the legendary campaign has a mechanic thats used for day one raids: Contest mode. You are locked under level by like 10 levels i think. it can get you close to current level tho.  Bright Engrams are not gone, they're given out in the battle pass and are a reward past level 100 for every 5 levels achieved. They are however not the only way of getting eververse shit for free. Bright Dust is the free store currency given out in the battle pass and as a reward for completing seasonal challenges.  The point at which you really understand the game is probably when you get into build crafting because theres a deceptively large amount of depth to build crafting. If you visit Ada every day you can pick up the mods she sells. The "Combat Style" mods are really where its at. Understanding how charged with light and elemental wells work is the first step in creating builds where your abilities are almost never on cooldown, you can demolish champions in seconds, and you're unkillable.   To give you an example i have a Stasis build for Titans i call "I AM THE FUCKING WALL!". I use the Hoarfrost-Z exotic chest which turns my titan barricade into a wall of stasis crystals and i have the subclass set up with a glacier grenade and all my fragments and aspects help with ability regen and survivability. Being near crystals increases ability regen and breaking crystals spawns shards that refill my melee and either give me overshield or start health regen. On top of that being near crystals gives me a damage reduction. My mods are set up so Stasis Shards count as Elemental wells (Elemental Shards is the mod. Wells refill ability energy.) but i also have a mod that boosts that effect essentially (Well of Restoration}. On top of that, picking up elemental wells makes me Charged With Light, picking up a well matching my subclass gives me 2 stacks (Elemental Charge) and combined with the mod Firepower being Charged with light when i use my grenade i get half of it back, consuming 1 stack of charged with light. I also have Utility Kickstart x2 which gives me a bit of my barricade charge back when i use my barricade. On top of all this i have 100 Resilience and 100 Discipline which gives me the lowest possible cooldown on my barricade and grenade respectively. Once you can understand what all of what i just said means and how to do this stuff yourself, you've basically mastered a good portion of the game.   Also good news, Bungie went on record saying they will not be vaulting anymore yearly expansions. Seasonal content will go away after the year is up but none of that gear gets sunset or anything. This also includes at least four other alien armies that decided to collectively kick our skulls in at around the same time of something called the collapse.  While humanity goes through a unga bunga cave man era, warlords are stealing stuff, and necromancer immortals start popping up in the bodies of robots with feelings. Eventually unga bunga time is over, humanity makes contact with a purple British human empire of a queen led people from space.  Now that humanity is mostly collected, we got a twitter user called The Witness who's seen too much twitter furry feet art and he wants to destroy everything. He's also a politician and he tricks an entire race of clam people to forsake their cancer and adapt to cringe, therefore becoming the witnesses servants.  Time skip: Big Russian robot hates aliens and wants to protect humanity, but humanity hates big robot because Russian bad. The chosen one goes to save big robot on red planet since there's a Alaskan bull worm there and its a god of the clam people. End story, mostly everybody used glitches to beat it in high ranked strikes.  Time skip: There's this warlock who's king of the nerds and he's a gay lover of this other dude who's a Russian robot, no this is a different Russian robot. Anyways, Nerd king gets lost, his lover is dead and we fix both problems by finding him and using funky wunky magic to go back in time and telling russian robot that dying is not gay. He now doesn't die.  Time skip: Queen of the purple British people has lost control of her prison known as England and she needs us to stop the four armed nerds inside who don't wanna pay taxes. The queen's step bro shoots our most valuable clown and single handily angers a powerful group of necromancers and assures his death within 24 hours of the DLCs release.
